</div>
			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">1982–83 Football League</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><table class="infobox" style="width:22em">
<caption><a href="/wiki/The_Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="The Football League">The Football League</a></caption>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Season</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/1982%E2%80%9383_in_English_football" title="1982–83 in English football">1982–83</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Champions</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="float: left;">← <a href="/wiki/1981%E2%80%9382_Football_League" title="1981–82 Football League">1981–82</a></div>
<div style="float: right;"><a href="/wiki/1983%E2%80%9384_Football_League" title="1983–84 Football League">1983–84</a> →</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>The <a href="/wiki/1982_in_association_football" title="1982 in association football">1982</a>–<a href="/wiki/1983_in_association_football" title="1983 in association football">1983</a> season</b> was the 84th completed season of <a href="/wiki/The_Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="The Football League">The Football League</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bob_Paisley" title="Bob Paisley">Bob Paisley</a>’s last season as <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> manager ended on a high as they topped the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">First Division</a> with a comfortable lead. Bob Paisley retired as Liverpool manager with a record 21 prizes in nine years. His successor was long-serving coach Joe Fagan. Newly promoted <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a> were the shock of the season, finishing in second place in their first ever season in the top flight.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> were relegated despite a four-year spending spree totalling around £5million. <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Swansea City F.C.">Swansea City</a> were also relegated after only their second season as a First Division club. They had finished sixth a year earlier and at several stages had topped the league table. <a href="/wiki/Brighton_%26_Hove_Albion_F.C." title="Brighton &amp; Hove Albion F.C.">Brighton &amp; Hove Albion</a> joined them on the way down.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wolverhampton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Wolverhampton Wanderers F.C.">Wolverhampton Wanderers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a> won promotion to the First Division. <a href="/wiki/Rotherham_United_F.C." title="Rotherham United F.C.">Rotherham United</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burnley_F.C." title="Burnley F.C.">Burnley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bolton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Bolton Wanderers F.C.">Bolton Wanderers</a> were relegated to the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division" title="Football League Third Division">Third Division</a>. It was another blow for Bolton, who had been relegated from the First Division three years earlier.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Charlton_Athletic_F.C." title="Charlton Athletic F.C.">Charlton Athletic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wolverhampton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Wolverhampton Wanderers F.C.">Wolverhampton Wanderers</a> both came within hours of going bankrupt but were both saved by respective new owners.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a>’s revival continued as they ran away with the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division" title="Football League Third Division">Third Division</a> championship, followed closely behind by runners-up <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a> and third-placed <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Town_A.F.C." title="Huddersfield Town A.F.C.">Huddersfield Town</a>. <a href="/wiki/Newport_County_A.F.C." title="Newport County A.F.C.">Newport County</a> finished 4th, their highest post-<a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> position in the Football League. Occupying the four <a href="/wiki/Relegation" class="mw-redirect" title="Relegation">relegation</a> places were <a href="/wiki/Reading_F.C." title="Reading F.C.">Reading</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wrexham_A.F.C." title="Wrexham A.F.C.">Wrexham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doncaster_Rovers_F.C." title="Doncaster Rovers F.C.">Doncaster Rovers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chesterfield_F.C." title="Chesterfield F.C.">Chesterfield</a>.</p>
<p>Wimbledon were crowned <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Fourth_Division" title="Football League Fourth Division">Fourth Division</a> champions and the efforts of manager <a href="/wiki/Dave_Bassett" title="Dave Bassett">Dave Bassett</a> were bound to ensure that this would not be their last promotion. <a href="/wiki/Hull_City_A.F.C." title="Hull City A.F.C.">Hull City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_Vale_F.C." title="Port Vale F.C.">Port Vale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scunthorpe_United_F.C." title="Scunthorpe United F.C.">Scunthorpe United</a> occupied the other three promotion places. The re-election system once again went in favour of the bottom four sides in the Fourth Division, but had things gone differently then <a href="/wiki/Blackpool_F.C." title="Blackpool F.C.">Blackpool</a> could have gone out of <a href="/wiki/The_Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="The Football League">the Football League</a> little over a decade after they had been a First Division side.</p>
<p>At the end of the season, Fourth Division strugglers <a href="/wiki/Crewe_Alexandra_F.C." title="Crewe Alexandra F.C.">Crewe Alexandra</a> appointed Milan-born ex-Wimbledon manager Dario Gradi as their new manager.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Final_league_tables_and_results">Final league tables and results</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1982%E2%80%9383_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Final league tables and results">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The tables and results below are reproduced here in the exact form that they can be found at <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.rsssf.com/engpaul/FLA/1982-83.html">The Rec.Sport.Soccer Statistics Foundation</a> website,<sup id="cite_ref-rsssf_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf-1">[1]</a></sup> with home and away statistics separated.</p>
<p>During the first five seasons of the league, that is, until the season 1893–94, re-election process concerned the clubs which finished in the bottom four of the league. From the 1894–95 season and until the 1920–21 season the re-election process was required of the clubs which finished in the bottom three of the league. From the 1922–23 season on it was required of the bottom two teams of both Third Division North and Third Division South. Since the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Fourth_Division" title="Football League Fourth Division">Fourth Division</a> was established in the <a href="/wiki/1958%E2%80%9359_Football_League" title="1958–59 Football League">1958–59 season</a>, the re-election process has concerned the bottom four clubs in that division.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Election.2FRe-election_to_the_Football_League">Election/Re-election to the Football League</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1982%E2%80%9383_Football_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Election/Re-election to the Football League">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>This year <a href="/wiki/Enfield_F.C." title="Enfield F.C.">Enfield</a>, the winners of the <a href="/wiki/Football_Conference" class="mw-redirect" title="Football Conference">Alliance Premier League</a>, could not apply for election because they did not meet Football League requirements, so 2nd placed <a href="/wiki/Maidstone_United_F.C._(1897)" title="Maidstone United F.C. (1897)">Maidstone United (1897)</a> won the right to apply for election to the Football League to replace one of the four bottom sides in the 1982–83 <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Fourth_Division" title="Football League Fourth Division">Football League Fourth Division</a>. The vote went as follows:</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:left;">
<tr>
<th width="140">Club</th>
<th width="185">Final Position</th>
<th width="50">Votes</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Blackpool_F.C." title="Blackpool F.C.">Blackpool</a></td>
<td>21st (Fourth Division)</td>
<td align="center">52</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Crewe_Alexandra_F.C." title="Crewe Alexandra F.C.">Crewe Alexandra</a></td>
<td>23rd (Fourth Division)</td>
<td align="center">49</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Hereford_United_F.C." title="Hereford United F.C.">Hereford United</a></td>
<td>24th (Fourth Division)</td>
<td align="center">49</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Hartlepool_United_F.C." title="Hartlepool United F.C.">Hartlepool United</a></td>
<td>22nd (Fourth Division)</td>
<td align="center">36</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Maidstone_United_F.C._(1897)" title="Maidstone United F.C. (1897)">Maidstone United (1897)</a></td>
<td>2nd (Alliance Premier League)</td>
<td align="center">26</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>As a result of this, all four Football League teams were re-elected, and <a href="/wiki/Maidstone_United_F.C._(1897)" title="Maidstone United F.C. (1897)">Maidstone United (1897)</a> were denied membership of the League.</p>
